25:T2861,<entryFree id="n7936" key="حَسَبَهُ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <itype>1</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">حَسَبَهُ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">حسب</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">حسبه</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">حسبة</orth>
                  </form>, (S, A, Mgh, &amp;c.,) aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bu" lang="ar">حَسُبَ</orth>
                  </form>, (S, Mgh, Msb, &amp;c.,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">حَسْبٌ</foreign> (S, A, Mgh, Msb, K) and <foreign lang="ar">حُسْبَانٌ</foreign> (S, Mgh, Msb, K) and <foreign lang="ar">حِسْبَانٌ</foreign> (K) and <foreign lang="ar">حِسَابٌ</foreign> (S, K,) which is generally an inf. n. of this verb, but sometimes of <foreign lang="ar">حَاسَبَ</foreign>, (TA,) and <foreign lang="ar">حِسَابَةٌ</foreign> (S, K) and <foreign lang="ar">حِسْبَةٌ</foreign>, (Msb, K,) or this is like <foreign lang="ar">قِعْدَةٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">رِكْبَةٌ</foreign>, [denoting a mode, or manner,] as in a verse of En-Nábighah cited below, (S,) and <foreign lang="ar">حَسْبَةٌ</foreign>, which is of rare occurrence, (MF, TA,) <hi rend="ital">He numbered, counted, reckoned, calculated,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">computed, it;</hi> (S, A, Mgh, Msb, K;) namely, property [&amp;c.]. (A, Mgh, Msb.) You say, <foreign lang="ar">مَنْ يَقْدِرُ عَلَى عَدِّ الرَّمْلِ وَحَسْبِ الحَصَى</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Who can count the sands, and number the pebbles?</hi>]. (A.) And <foreign lang="ar">أَلْقِ هٰذَا فِى الحَسْبِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Throw thou this into the reckoning</hi>]; i. e., <hi rend="ital">into what thou hast reckoned.</hi> (A.) <foreign lang="ar">وَالشَّمْسُ وَالقَمَرُ بِحُسْبَانٍ</foreign>, in the Kur [lv. 4], means <hi rend="ital">And the sun and the moon</hi> [run their courses] <hi rend="ital">according to a</hi> [certain] <hi rend="ital">reckoning;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">through a series of mansions</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">constellations</hi>], the bounds of which they do not transgress: (TA:) or <foreign lang="ar">بحسبان</foreign> alludes to the numbers of the months and years and all other times: [but properly speaking,] <foreign lang="ar">حسبان</foreign> is here an inf. n.: (Zj, TA:) or, accord. to Akh, a pl. of <foreign lang="ar">حِسَابٌ</foreign>; (S, TA;) and so says AHeyth: or, accord. to some, it is here a proper subst., signifying the <hi rend="ital">firmament.</hi> (TA.) <foreign lang="ar">حُسْبَانًا</foreign> in the Kur vi. 96 is held by Akh to be for <foreign lang="ar">بِحُسْبَانٍ</foreign>, meaning <foreign lang="ar">بِحِسَابٍ</foreign> [as in the phrase quoted above, from the Kur lv. 4, accord. to the first explanation]. (TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">حُسْبَانُكَ عَلَى ٱللّٰه</foreign> signifies <foreign lang="ar">حِسَابُكَ على اللّٰه</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">On</hi> 
                  <pb n="565"/> 
                  <hi rend="ital">God be it to reckon with thee:</hi> see also <foreign lang="ar">حَسِيبُكَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">ٱللّٰهُ</foreign>]. (TA.) Az says that the reckoning in buying and selling is termed <foreign lang="ar">حِسَابٌ</foreign> because one knows thereby what is sufficient. (TA.) <foreign lang="ar">وَٱللّٰهُ سَرِيعُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الحِسَابِ</foreign>, in the Kur [ii. 198, &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">God is quick in reckoning</hi>], signifies that his reckoning is necessary, or of necessity, and that his reckoning with one person does not divert Him from reckoning with another. (TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">يَرْزُقُ مَنْ يَشَآءُ بَغَيْرِ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">حِسَابٍ</foreign>, in the Kur [ii. 208, &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">He supplieth whom He willeth, without reckoning</hi>], means <hi rend="ital">without sparing,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">scanting;</hi> as when a man expends without reckoning: but the phrase is variously explained, as meaning <hi rend="ital">without appointing for any one what is deficient:</hi> or <hi rend="ital">without fearing that any one will call Him to account for it:</hi> or <hi rend="ital">without the receiver's thinking that He will bestow upon him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">without his reckoning upon the supply;</hi> so that it may be from <foreign lang="ar">حَسِبَ</foreign> “ he thought, ” or from <foreign lang="ar">حَسَبَ</foreign> “ he reckoned. ” (L, TA.) The saying, cited by IAar, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">يَا جُمْلُ أَسْقَاكِ بِلَا حِسَابَهْ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> as related by J [in the S], but correctly <foreign lang="ar">أُسْقيت</foreign>, (TA,) means [<hi rend="ital">O Juml, mayest thou be given rain</hi>] <hi rend="ital">without reckoning,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">without measure.</hi> (S.) An instance of <foreign lang="ar">حِسْبَةٌ</foreign> as similar to <foreign lang="ar">قِعْدَةٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">رِكْبَةٌ</foreign> occurs in the saying of En-Nábighah, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">فَكَمَّلَتْ مِائَةً فِيهَا حَمَامَتُهَا</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">وَأَسْرَعَتْ حسْبَةً فِى ذٰلِكَ العَدَدٍ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">And she completed a hundred, in which was her pigeon; and she was quick in the mode of computing that number</hi>]. (S.)       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">حَسِبَهُ كَذَا</foreign>, [a verb of the kind termed <foreign lang="ar">أَفْعَالُ القُلُوبِ</foreign>, having two objective complements, the former of which is called its noun, and the latter its enunciative,] aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Ba" lang="ar">حَسَبَ</orth>
                  </form> and      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bi" lang="ar">حَسِبَ</orth>
                  </form>; (S, Msb, K;) the former the more approved, (TA,) of the dialects of all the Arabs except Benoo-Kináneh; the latter aor. being peculiar to the dial. of this tribe, (Msb,) and contr. to analogy, (S, Msb,) for by rule it should be      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Ba" lang="ar">حَسَبَ</orth>
                  </form> [only]; and <foreign lang="ar">حَسِبَ</foreign> is the only verb of the measure <foreign lang="ar">فَعِلَ</foreign> having both <foreign lang="ar">يَفْعَلُ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">يَفْعِلُ</foreign> as the measures of its aor. except <foreign lang="ar">نَعِمَ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">يَئِسَ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">يَبِسَ</foreign> [and <foreign lang="ar">وَعِر َ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">وَحِرَ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">بَئِسَ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">وَلِهَ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">وَهِلَ</foreign> mentioned by Ibn-Málik (with the preceding) cited in the TA voce <foreign lang="ar">وَرِثَ</foreign>]; but eight verbs having an unsound letter for the first radical have kesreh to the medial radical in the pret. and aor., viz., <foreign lang="ar">وَثِقَ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">وَرِثَ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">وَرِعَ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">وَرِمَ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">وَرِيَ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">وَفِقَ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">وَلِىَ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">وَمِقَ</foreign>; (S;) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">حِسْبَانٌ</foreign> (S, Mgh, Msb, K) and <foreign lang="ar">مَحْسَبَةٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">مَحْسِبَةٌ</foreign> (S, K) and <foreign lang="ar">حِسَابٌ</foreign>; (TA; [but see what follows;]) <hi rend="ital">He</hi> [<hi rend="ital">counted, accounted, reckoned,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">esteemed,</hi> meaning] <hi rend="ital">thought,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">supposed, him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it, to be so.</hi> (S, Mgh, Msb, K.) You say, <foreign lang="ar">حَسِبْتُهُ صَالِحًا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I counted him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">thought him, good,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">righteous</hi>]. (S.) And <foreign lang="ar">حَسِبْتُ زَيْدًا قَائِمًا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I thought Zeyd to be standing</hi>]. (Msb.) And <foreign lang="ar">مَا كَانَ فِى حِسْبَانِى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">كَذَا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Such a thing was not in my thought</hi>]: you should not say <foreign lang="ar">فى حِسَابِى</foreign>, (K,) unless you mean thereby <hi rend="ital">it was not included in my reckoning,</hi> or, by amplification of the sense, <hi rend="ital">I did not think it.</hi> (MF.)       <sense type="A" n="3">-A3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">حَسُبَ</foreign>, aor.

[Hence,] <foreign lang="ar">احتسب وَلَدَهُ</foreign>, (A, Mgh,) or <foreign lang="ar">ٱبْنَهُ</foreign>, (Msb,) or <foreign lang="ar">ٱبْنًا</foreign>, or <foreign lang="ar">بنْتًا</foreign>, (S, K, *) is said when one has lost by death an adult child or son or daughter; (S, A, Mgh, Msb, K;) meaning <hi rend="ital">He prepared,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">provided, in store for himself, a reward, by his patience on the occasion of his being afflicted and tried by the death of his adult child:</hi> (Mgh, * TA:) when a man has lost by death a child not arrived at the age of puberty, you say of him, <foreign lang="ar">اِفْتَرَطَهُ</foreign>.                   <hi rend="ital">Sufficiency.</hi> (K voce <foreign lang="ar">هَسْبٌ</foreign>.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">حَسْبُ</foreign> is a [prefixed] noun (S) [syn. with <foreign lang="ar">كَفْىُ</foreign>, as is implied in the K voce <foreign lang="ar">قَطْ</foreign>; or] syn. with <foreign lang="ar">كَافِى</foreign>; (Msb;) or [virtually] meaning <foreign lang="ar">كَفَى</foreign> [as a pret. in the sense of an emphatic aor.]; (S, K;) or <foreign lang="ar">يَكْفِى</foreign>: (TA:) Sb says that it is used to denote the being sufficed, or content. (TA.) You say, <foreign lang="ar">حَسْبُكَ دِرْهَمٌ</foreign> [and <foreign lang="ar">بِحَسْبِكَ دِرْهَمٌ</foreign>, in which latter the <foreign lang="ar">ب</foreign> is redundant; meaning <hi rend="ital">Thy sufficiency,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">a thing sufficing thee, is a dirhem;</hi> a phrase which may be used in two ways; as predicating of what is sufficient, that it is a dirhem; and as predicating of a dirhem, that it is sufficient; in which latter case, <foreign lang="ar">بحسبك</foreign> is an enunciative put before its inchoative, (as also <foreign lang="ar">حَسْبُكَ</foreign>,) so that the meaning is, <hi rend="ital">a dirhem is a thing sufficing thee,</hi> i. e. <hi rend="ital">a dirhem is sufficient for thee;</hi> as is shown in a marginal note in my copy of the Mughnee, in art. <foreign lang="ar">بِ</foreign>; or, accord. to the S and K, <hi rend="ital">a dirhem suffices thee:</hi> accord. to Bd (iii. 167), <foreign lang="ar">بحسبك</foreign> means <foreign lang="ar">مُحْسِبُكَ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">كَافِيكَ</foreign>, from <foreign lang="ar">أَحْسَبَهُ</foreign> meaning <foreign lang="ar">كَفَاهُ</foreign>; and is shown to have this meaning by its not importing a determinate signification in consequence of its being a prefixed noun with its complement in the saying, <foreign lang="ar">هٰذَا رَجُلٌ حَسْبُكَ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">This is a man sufficing thee</hi>]. (S, Msb, K.) You say also, <foreign lang="ar">حَسْبُكَ ذٰلِكَ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">That is,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">will be,</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">let that be,</hi>] <hi rend="ital">sufficient for thee.</hi> (TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">حَسْبُكَ ٱللّٰهُ</foreign>, in the Kur viii. 65, <hi rend="ital">God is,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">will be, sufficient for thee.</hi> (Fr, TA. See also <foreign lang="ar">حَسِيبُكَ ٱللّٰهُ</foreign>.) And <foreign lang="ar">حَسْبُكَ بِصَدِيقِنَا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">A person sufficing thee is our friend</hi>]; in which the <foreign lang="ar">ب</foreign> is added to denote emphatic praise. (Fr, TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">بِ</foreign>.) In the saying, <foreign lang="ar">هٰذَا رَجُلٌ حَسْبُكَ مِنْ رَجُلٍ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">This is a man sufficing thee as a man,</hi> i. e. <hi rend="ital">supplying to thee the place of any other</hi> [by his excellent qualities], (S, K,) and <foreign lang="ar">مَرَرْتُ بِرَجُلٍ حَسْبِكَ مِنْ رَجُلٍ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">I passed by a man sufficing thee as a man,</hi> (TA,) <foreign lang="ar">حسبك</foreign> is an expression of praise, referring to the indeterminate noun [<foreign lang="ar">رجل</foreign>]; because, in its case, [what is originally (see below)] an inf. n. (<foreign lang="ar">فِعْلٌ</foreign> [under which term lexicologists, but not grammarians, include the <foreign lang="ar">مَصْدَر</foreign>]) is rendered, in grammatical analysis, by another word, [i. e., by an act. part. n.,] as though one said <foreign lang="ar">مُحْسِبٌ لَكَ</foreign>, or <foreign lang="ar">كَافٍ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">لَكَ</foreign>. (S. [Thus <foreign lang="ar">حسبك</foreign> in these two instances is a <foreign lang="ar">صِفَة</foreign>, i. e. an epithetic phrase; and <foreign lang="ar">من رجل</foreign> is a <foreign lang="ar">تَمْيِيز</foreign>, i. e. a specificative phrase.]) When the noun to which <foreign lang="ar">حسبك</foreign> refers is determinate, you put <foreign lang="ar">حسب</foreign> in the accus. case, as a <foreign lang="ar">حال</foreign>, i. e. a denotative of state; as in the saying, <foreign lang="ar">هٰذَا عَبْدُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">ٱللّٰهِ حَسْبَكَ مِنْ رَجُلٍ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">This is 'Abd-Allah; being one sufficing thee as a man.</hi> (S. [Here <foreign lang="ar">من رجل</foreign> is, as before, a specificative phrase.]) [See also 4, the corresponding verb.]) <foreign lang="ar">حسب</foreign>, in this manner, is used alike as sing. and dual and pl.; (S, K;) being [originally] an inf. n. (S.) It is also used alone, [as a prefixed noun of which the complement is understood,] as in the phrase <foreign lang="ar">زَيْدٌ حَسْبُ</foreign>, without tenween, for <foreign lang="ar">حَسْبِى</foreign> or <foreign lang="ar">حَسْبُكَ</foreign> [&amp;c., meaning <hi rend="ital">Zeyd is sufficient for me</hi> or <hi rend="ital">for thee</hi> &amp;c.]; like as one says, <foreign lang="ar">جَآءَنِى زَيْدٌ لَيْسَ غَيْرُ</foreign>, for <foreign lang="ar">لَيْسَ غَيْرُهُ عِنْدِى</foreign>. (S. [That is, <foreign lang="ar">حَسْبُ</foreign>, when thus used, is subject to the same rules as <foreign lang="ar">غَيْرُ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">قَبْلُ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">بَعْدُ</foreign> &amp;c. when so used.])          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  See also <foreign lang="ar">حَسَبٌ</foreign>, in three places.       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  Also, (TA,) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n7943-1" target="حِسْبَةٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n7946"/></foreign>, (K,) <hi rend="ital">Burial</hi> of the dead: (TA:) or <hi rend="ital">burial</hi> of the dead <hi rend="ital">in stones</hi> [app. meaning <hi rend="ital">in a grave cased with stones</hi>]: or <hi rend="ital">burial</hi> of the dead <hi rend="ital">wrapped in grave-clothes:</hi> like <foreign lang="ar">تَحْسِيبٌ</foreign>. (K. [See 2.])    </entryFree>2b:T1d3c,<entryFree id="n7944" key="حَسَبٌ" type="main">

                  <hi rend="ital">i. q.</hi>   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n7944-1" target="مَحْسُوبٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="SO" lang="ar" select="n7957"/></foreign>; (S, K;) of the measure <foreign lang="ar">فَعَلٌ</foreign> in the sense of the measure <foreign lang="ar">مَفْعُولٌ</foreign>, like <foreign lang="ar">نَفَضٌ</foreign> in the sense of <foreign lang="ar">مَنْفُوضٌ</foreign>; (S;) <hi rend="ital">Numbered, counted, reckoned, calculated,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">computed.</hi> (S, K.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <hi rend="ital">A number counted.</hi> (L.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <hi rend="ital">Amount, quantity,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">value.</hi> (L.) Sometimes, (S, L, K,) by poetic license, (S,) and in prose, (L,)
